#### 10.7.2.10 Power Management
##### 10.7.2.10.1 Clock Gating
Refer to the "Clock Gates" section.

MACsec Programming Guidelines
##### 10.7.2.10.2 Power Gating
Either the whole MGBE_wrapper or the ETHER_QOS wrapper can be power gated. There is no standalone power gating for MACsec.
##### 10.7.2.10.3 Cold/Warm Boot
The behavior of MACsec remains the same during either cold or warm Boot. MACsec needs to go through the same reset sequence with other modules in MGBE_wrapper or ETHER_QOS wrapper module.
### 10.7.3 MACsec Programming Guidelines
#### 10.7.3.1 Initial Configuration Guidelines
##### 10.7.3.1.1 Clocks and Reset Programming
1. 2. Assert MACsec Clock enables. Refer to the "Clocks" section for details. Apply and release MACsec Resets. Refer to the "Resets" section for the register names.
##### 10.7.3.1.2 Global Configuration Programming Guidelines
Refer to the "Global Configuration Register Fields Description" section for the following register bits: 1. Enable the following interrupts. These are the basic set interrupts required for MACsec Operation. a. MACSEC_TX_INTERRUPT_MASK_0 i. PN_EXHAUSTED_INT_EN PN_THRSHLD_RCHD_INT_EN AES_GCM_BUF_OVF_INT_EN ii. iii. b. MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_MASK_0 i. PN_EXHAUSTED_INT_EN REPLAY_ERROR_INT_EN ICV_ERROR_INT_EN AES_GCM_BUF_OVF_INT_EN ii. iii. iv. c. MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK0_0 i. RX_UNINIT_KEY_SLOT_INT_EN RX_LKUP_MISS_INT_EN TX_UNINIT_KEY_SLOT_INT_EN ii. iii.

MACsec Programming Guidelines iv. TX_LKUP_MISS_INT_EN d. MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK1_0 i. SFTY_ERR_UNCORR_INT_EN 2. 3. Program the MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.VALIDATE_FRAMES field based on the use case. Enable or disable replay protection based on the use case, by programming the MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_REPLAY_PROT_EN field. a. If replay protection is enabled, enable the corresponding interrupt using the MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_MASK_0.REPLAY_ERROR_INT_EN register field. 4. Assign priority between Tx SC Index and Tx Bypass LUTs. It is used in the case a packet makes a hit in both LUTs. This can be programmed using the bit MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.TX_LUT_PRIORITY. Enable/Disable MTU Check unit in MACsec based on the use case, by programming the following fields. 5. MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.TX_MTU_CHECK_ENB MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.RX_MTU_CHECK_ENB 6. If MTU Check is enabled, program the following fields with the MTU threshold value that is, with value: MAC MTU+SECTAG size+ICV size. If the packet length exceeds this threshold value, MTU check will fail and the corresponding interrupt is asserted. Refer to the "MTU Check on Egress and Ingress Packets" section for more details on MTU Check. MACSEC_TX_MTU_LEN_0[15:0] MACSEC_RX_MTU_LEN_0[15:0] 7. If MTU Check is enabled, also enable the corresponding interrupts using the following register bits: MACSEC_TX_INTERRUPT_MASK_0.MTU_CHECK_FAIL_INT_EN MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_MASK_0.MTU_CHECK_FAIL_INT_EN 8. Program the AES GCM Engine Mode to 128/256 bit Key, using the following register fields. MACSEC_GCM_AES_CONTROL_0. TX_AES_MODE MACSEC_GCM_AES_CONTROL_0. RX_AES_MODE 9. Program the following fields if nonsecure interrupt should be asserted for Tx/Rx lookup miss events. By default, secure interrupt is asserted when such events happen. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.TX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR 10. Enable double VLAN processing, program the DVLAN_CONTROL_0 registers, and choose between the inner or outer VLAN fields for LUT lookup. Refer the "Handling VLAN Packets" section for details. Enable the necessary Tx and Rx Bypass LUT entries by programming 1 in the following register fields. The following registers are 32-bit in size. Each bit corresponds to the validity of each LUT entry. (1-> Valid LUT Entry, 0-> Invalid LUT Entry) 11. MACSEC_TX_BYP_LUT_VALID MACSEC_RX_BYP_LUT_VALID

MACsec Programming Guidelines Hardware does the lookup only in the Valid LUT Entries. Enable the necessary Tx and Rx SC_INDEX LUT entries by programming 1 in the following register fields. The following registers are 16 bit in size. Each bit corresponds to the validity of each LUT entry. (1-> Valid LUT Entry, 0-> Invalid LUT Entry) 12. MACSEC_TX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID_0 MACSEC_RX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID_0 Hardware does the lookup only in the Valid LUT Entries.
##### 10.7.3.1.3 Guidelines to Bypass MACsec Functionality for MKPDU Traffic
Software must populate Tx and Rx Bypass LUTs to bypass the MACsec functionality for specific ethernet traffic. Description of Tx and Rx Bypass LUTs is present in these sections "Description of Egress Lookup Tables" and "Description of MACsec Ingress Lookup Tables" respectively. Populate Tx and Rx Bypass LUT entries with the parameters of MKPDU Traffic (for example, MAC_SA, MAC_DA, EtherType). Steps to configure the LUTs are described in the "Configuring MACsec LUTs" section. Program the lookup result of the LUT entry to uncontrolled port. Program bit field [205:205] of the LUT entry to 0. Program Valid bit in respective register depending on LUT programmed. - - MACSEC_TX_BYP_LUT_VALID_0 MACSEC_RX_BYP_LUT_VALID_0 Software should program only the required entries, for others set the valid bit to zero. Software can configure multiple such entries. If the packet hits multiple entries, the hardware takes the lowest index-entry lookup result. .
##### 10.7.3.1.4 Guidelines to Create a Secure Channel in MACsec Tx
Tx SC INDEX, Tx SC_PARAMETER, Tx SC_STATE, Tx SA_STATE, and Tx KEY_TABLE LUT must be programmed for creating a secure channel in MACsec Tx. Note: A LUT entry is only programmed for valid entries. For others, software should ensure to put the valid bit as “0” to invalidate the entry. The description of these LUTs is present in the "Description of Egress Lookup Tables" section. Steps to configure these LUTs are present in the "Configuring MACsec LUTs" section. Tx SC INDEX LUT Programming

MACsec Programming Guidelines Using this LUT, software provides the secure channel index (SC_INDEX) and corresponding valid ANs to hardware for protecting ethernet traffic with certain parameters (MAC_DA, MAC_SA, EtherType). - - Populate each SC_INDEX LUT entry with the parameters of the ethernet traffic. Populate lookup results for each SC_INDEX LUT entry. That is: SC_INDEX field–Bits[212:209] Valid AN field–Bits[208:205] Make the corresponding entry valid by programming Valid bit in respective register: MACSEC_TX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID_0 MACSEC_RX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID_0 If the incoming traffic hits multiple entries, lowest index lookup results are used by hardware for further processing. Tx SC PARAMETER LUT Programming Software populates the following parameters in the LUT, for each secure channel (SC_INDEX). Hardware requires these for MACsec Processing. - TCI, SCI, KEY_INDEX_START, VLAN_IN_CLR, PN_MAX, PN_TRHESHOLD - As shown in the Egress Lookup Flow Diagram, each row of this LUT gives parameters of a particular SC_INDEX (for example, row#0 gives parameters of SC_INDEX0, row1-> parameters of SC_INDEX1,…). - Software must program the parameters in the LUT at each SC_INDEX offset. - TCI field should be programmed as: V = 0/1 ES = 0 or 1 depending on the platform requirements - - ES=1 if first six octets of SCI are MAC SA ES=0 if MAC SA is not used to determine SCI SC = 0 or 1 depending on following requirements - - SC=0 if SCI is not present in SecTAG or ES=1 SC=1 if SCI is explicitly encoded (MACsec standard [1] (IEEE 802.1AE_2018). Section 9.9) {ES, SC} valid encodings are {00,01,10} The following TCI bits are tied off in hardware as: - - - SCB=0 E=0 C=0 - SCI field It is an 8-byte field. It should be programmed as defined in MACsec standard [1] (IEEE 802.1AE_2018). Note: Even for the case (ES =1, SC =0), software should populate SCI LUT field with the correct value. In this case, SCI = {SA, 0x0001}.

MACsec Programming Guidelines - KEY_INDEX_START As shown in the Egress Lookup Flow Diagram, KEY_INDEX_START is used to point to the start of secure channel keys in the Key Table. Hence, software should program this field accordingly. - VLAN_IN_CLR Based on this bit value, SecTag header will be added before or after VLAN field. Software must program this bit based on the use case. - PN_MAX and PN_THRESHOLD Software must program these fields for the given secure channel and the initial AN that is populated in the TX SC STATE Table. Note: If the ES and SC bits of TCI are set to 1 due to some programming error. This following is the hardware behavior. a. b. SecTag is added without SCI [with SC =1 and ES=1] ICV is added. Packet is NOT corrupted. c. Tx SC STATE LUT Programming It contains only one field CURRENT_AN[1:0]. Stores the CURRENT_AN info for each SC. As shown in Egress Lookup Flow Diagram, each row of the LUT represents CURRENT_AN field of SC_INDEX[row#]. Software initializes this field with the starting AN value for each SC Index. Software and hardware controls this table. Hardware uses it for frame processing and when the PN of the current AN saturates, hardware updates the field with the next AN Value. Tx SA STATE LUT Programming This LUT contains two fields: NEXT_PN and VALID Software should initialize NEXT_PN and VALID bits for each SA (secure association) entry, as shown in Egress Lookup Flow Diagram. Hardware uses this NEXT_PN field to populate the PN field in the SECTAG of the MACsec frame. Hardware increments the NEXT_PN field (by 1) for every valid frame assigned to that SA (secure association). Hardware sets the VALID bit to 0. Once the PN value for that secure association reaches the PN_Max limit and moves to next valid SA. Software reinitializes the Next_PN and VALID bits. Software MUST initialize the next SA before the expiry of the previous one. If VALID=0, it means that the software owns the entry. Hardware does not use this entry. If VALID=1, hardware can use the entry. Tx Key Table Programming

MACsec Programming Guidelines This LUT contains 256/128 bit SAK, 128-bit H-Key, and a 1-bit VALID field. H-Key = ESAK(0128) is the Hash Key, a string of 128 zero bits encrypted using AES-GCM engine Software should populate the SAK and H-Key for all valid SCs and valid ANs. Software sets the VALID bit during Keys programming and hardware clears it when the corresponding PN saturates.
##### 10.7.3.1.5 Guidelines to Create a Secure Channel in MACsec Rx
Rx SC INDEX, Rx SC_PARAMETER, Rx SC_STATE, Rx SA_STATE, and Rx KEY_TABLE LUTs must be programmed for creating a secure channel in MACsec Rx. Program MACSEC_RX_SECTAG_CONFIG_0.TCI_V. Note that only “zero” setting is spec compliant as “one” setting ignores the version number in Security Tagged frames. Note: A LUT entry is only programmed for Valid entries. For others, software should make sure to put Valid bit as “0” to invalidate the entry. Description of these LUTs is present in the "Description of MACsec Ingress Lookup Tables" section. Steps to configure these LUTs are present in the "Configuring MACsec LUTs" section. Rx SC INDEX LUT Programming Using this LUT, software provides the secure channel index info (SC_INDEX) to hardware for validating MACsec Ethernet Traffic with certain parameters (such as SCI, Prempted/ Non-Preempted traffic). Software must populate RX_SCINDEX LUT fields with the parameters of the MACsec Ethernet Traffic. Lookup result: SC_INDEX must be programmed at each offset and make the entry valid, by programming ENTRY_VALID field to 1. Hardware will compare the parameters of the incoming traffic with the fields of the LUT and determine the SC_Index (lookup result) for that particular packet. - - - Rx SC PARAMETER LUT Programming Similar to the Tx SC Parameter LUT, parameters in each row correspond to each SC_INDEX, as shown in Ingress Look Flow Diagram. Software must program: KEY_INDEX_START - to point to start of SC keys in the Key Table LUT. PN_WINDOW - If Rx needs to receive out of order packets.

MACsec Programming Guidelines - PN_MAX Mac Packet Number programmed Rx SA STATE LUT Programming Contains NEXT_PN, PN_MAX and LOWEST_PN fields Software initializes the NEXT_PN, PN_MAX and LOWEST_PN values for each secure association If replay protection is enabled (Global Configuration), MACsec hardware checks if the received pkt PN >= LOWEST_PN configured in this LUT. If this check fails, - - Received packets are corrupted and sent to MAC. Status is logged and a nonsecure interrupt is asserted. Refer to the "REPLAY_ERROR" section for more details. Hardware does update the NEXT_PN or the LOWEST_PN values in the LUT. - If the replay check passes (or if the check is not enabled) and once the packet has been successfully validated, hardware updates the NEXT_PN and LOWEST_PN values in the manner described in “Figure 10-4—Management controls and counters for secure frame verification” of IEEE 802.1AE_2018. Rx SC STATE LUT Programming Contains CURRENT_AN field. Hardware populates this field based on the current Rx MACsec Packet that it receives. Software can look at this register to know the current AN of the packet. Software does not need to write anything into this LUT. Rx Key Table LUT Programming Secure software must populate SAK, H-Key, and VALID fields for all valid SCs and valid ANs. Depending on Cipher suite mode (Refer to the "Global Configuration Register Fields Description" section), SAK field is programmed with a 128-bit key or a 256-bit key.
##### 10.7.3.1.6 SOT_Delay Settings for EQOS and MGBE
Program SOT_Delay settings as defined in the "SoT (Start of Transmission) Delay Setting" section. Note that he setting is different between EQOS and MGBE.
##### 10.7.3.1.7 Enable MACsec Tx and Rx Engines
After the preceding initial configuration is done, enable MACsec Tx and Rx Engines by programming the following bits. This enables MACsec Processing for the incoming packets. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0. TX_ENB=1 MACSEC_CONTROL0_0. RX_ENB=1

MACsec Programming Guidelines
#### 10.7.3.2 Run Time Configuration Guidelines
At runtime, MACsec hardware gives various interrupts. The following section gives details about the type of interrupts, why they occur, error logging info (status) for each interrupt and how to clear the interrupt.
##### 10.7.3.2.1 Interrupts Handling
MACsec has two interrupts. Secure Interrupt and Non-Secure Interrupt. Nonsecure interrupt gets asserted when the following events occur and when their corresponding interrupt enable bits are set to 1 in MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_MASK_0 registers. 1. Tx/Rx MTU Check Fail Tx SC_AN_NOT_VALID Tx/Rx MAC CRC ERROR Tx/Rx PN_EXHAUSTED Tx PN THRESHOLD REACHED Tx/Rx AES GCM BUFFER OVERFLOW Tx/Rx LKP MISS (Special case: Refer to the following note.) Tx/Rx DBG_BUF_CAPTURE_DONE ICV_ERROR REPLAY_ERROR Secure interrupt is asserted when the following events occur and when their corresponding interrupt enable bits are set to 1 in MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK0_0 register. 2. Non-TZ entity-accessing TZ registers. Use of uninitialized Tx/Rx Key-in Key Table LUT Tx/Rx LKP MISS Note: Tx/Rx LKP MISS event is a special case. Its interrupt mask is present in MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK0_0 register. By default, this event asserts secure interrupt. But if the register field MACSEC_CONTROL0.TX/RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=1, this event asserts nonsecure interrupt. Handling Non-Secure Interrupt 1. Read the MACSEC_INTERRUPT_COMMON_STATUS_0 register to know if it is a Tx or Rx interrupt. Read the MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0 register to find which interrupt causing events occurred. 2. If MACSEC_CONTROL0.TX/RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=1, TX/RX_LKUP_MISS event may also be the reason for Non-Secure interrupt assertion.

MACsec Programming Guidelines 3. Read MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_MASK_0 register to know the events that are enabled on the nonsecure interrupt line. Also read MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK0_0.TX/RX_LKUP_MISS_INT_EN register fields, if MACSEC_CONTROL0.TX/RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=1 4. The following sections describe error logging and interrupt clearing procedure for various events. Note: MACSEC_INTERRUPT_COMMON_STATUS_0 register is auto cleared after all the pending events (that cause secure and nonsecure interrupts) are handled. PN THRESHOLD This event indicates to software that the PN value of some SAs (Secure Associations) reached the threshold value. The SC and AN details of such secure associations are logged in these registers: MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_THRESHOLD_STATUS0_0, MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_THRESHOLD_STATUS1_0. Software can use this information to identify the SAs that are about to expire. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt Write 1 to the corresponding AN bit locations of MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_THRESHOLD_STATUS0_0 and MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_THRESHOLD_STATUS1_0 registers. This auto clears MACSEC_TX_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.PN_THRSHLD_RCHD register field. Nonsecure interrupt line will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. PN EXHAUSTED This event indicates to software that some SAs are expired. For example, PN value of the SAs reached the PN MAX value. The SC and AN details of the SAs that got expired, are logged in these registers: MACSEC_<TX/RX>_SC_PN_EXHAUSTED_STATUS0_0, MACSEC_<TX/ RX>_SC_PN_EXHAUSTED_STATUS1_0. If software wants to reuse these SAs, reenable the SAs by programming the Keys, NEXT_PN, and Valid bits in the SA_STATE and Key Table LUTs. Valid Bit is present in only Tx SA LUT but not in Rx. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt Write 1 to the corresponding AN bit locations of MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_EXHAUSTED_STATUS0_0 and MACSEC_TX_SC_PN_EXHAUSTED_STATUS1_0 registers. This auto clears MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.PN_EXHAUSTED register field. Nonsecure interrupt line will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. INVALID AN This event indicates that a particular SC hit an invalid entry in the Tx SA_STATE Table.

MACsec Programming Guidelines Read MACSEC_TX_SC_ERROR_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0 register to know the SCs that hit this error. Software must enable the ANs in advance, to avoid this kind of error. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to clear the corresponding SC bits in MACSEC_TX_SC_ERROR_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0 register. This auto clears MACSEC_TX_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.SC_AN_NOT_VALID bit. Nonsecure interrupt line will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. MAC CRC ERROR This interrupt gets asserted when there is a CRC error in the incoming pkt. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to clear MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.MAC_CRC_ERROR register field. Nonsecure interrupt line is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. MTU CHECK FAIL This interrupt is asserted when MACSEC_CONTROL1.<TX/RX>_MTU_CHECK_ENB register bit is enabled and when pkt length is greater than the maximum pkt size programmed in <TX/ RX>_MTU_LEN registers. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.MTU_CHECK_FAIL register field. Nonsecure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. ICV_ERROR This error occurs when the incoming ICV tag does not match with the calculated ICV tag at the Rx side. MACSEC_RX_SC_ICV_ERROR_STATUS_0 register logs the SC numbers, which encountered this error. And the status bit for each SC is set on the first occurrence of an ICV error in that SC. It has no relation to ICV threshold settings. And the status bits do not generate any interrupt. When the number of ICV errors exceed the threshold, programmed in MACSECRX_ICV_ERROR_CONTROL register, hardware triggers the nonsecure interrupt. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.ICV_ERROR bit field. Nonsecure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. The following table summarizes Interrupt plus Threshold count capabilities for various events.

MACsec Programming Guidelines Table 10.32 Interrupt and Threshold Count Capabilities Error Event Status Threshold Interrupt Stats Counter ICV Errors - Aggregate of all SCs Yes Yes Yes No ICV Errors per SC Yes No No Yes Replay Protection per SC Yes No Yes Yes CRC Errors in Received Pkt Yes No Yes MACSEC_TX_INPKTS_CRCIN_N OTVALID_LO/HI_0 MACSEC_RX_INPKTS_CRCIN_N OTVALID_LO/HI_0 Encrypted Packets in Ingress traffic No No No No Lookup Miss Yes No Yes Yes for "MACSEC tagged" packets: InPktsNoSAError No for Bypass "MACSEC untagged" RX: Non MACSEC Packets No No No Yes: InPktsNoTag RX: Bad MACSEC tags (SecTag, ICV) No No No Yes: InPktsBadTag REPLAY_ERROR This error occurs when MACSEC_CONTROL0.RX_REPLAY_PROT_EN=1 and when the incoming packets PN value is not within the permitted PN_window value. Details of the SCs and ANs, which failed the replay check are logged in MACSEC_RX_SC_REPLAY_ERROR_STATUS0_0 and MACSEC_RX_SC_REPLAY_ERROR_STATUS1_0 registers. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in the corresponding bit locations of MACSEC_RX_SC_REPLAY_ERROR_STATUS0_0 and MACSEC_RX_SC_REPLAY_ERROR_STATUS1_0 registers. This auto clears MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0.REPLAY_ERROR register. Nonsecure interrupt will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Tx Lookup Miss Interrupt This event occurs when there is no hit in both Tx BYPASS and SC LUT. This event can assert a nonsecure interrupt if MACSEC_CONTROL0.TX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=1. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in the MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.TX_LKUP_MISS register. Nonsecure interrupt will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Rx Lookup Miss Interrupt

MACsec Programming Guidelines This event occurs when there is no hit in Rx SC and BYPASS LUT. This event can assert a secure/non-secure interrupt if MACSEC_CONTROL0.RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=0/1. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in the MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.RX_LKUP_MISS register field. Nonsecure interrupt will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Debug Buffer Interrupt This event indicates to software, that the programmed trigger event has been hit and the corresponding packet has been captured in the debug buffer. The hit trigger event detail is logged in the register: MACSEC_<TX/RX>_DEBUG_STATUS_0. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to clear MACSEC_<TX/RX>_INTERRUPT_STATUS_0. DBG_BUF_CAPTURE_DONE register field. Nonsecure interrupt line will be de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Write 1 to clear the bit set in the MACSEC_<TX/RX>_DEBUG _STATUS_0 register. Handling Secure Interrupt Uninitialized Key in Tx/Rx Key Table LUT This occurs when an invalid/uninitialized key is attempted for use (for the ICV generation in the Tx Side and ICV validation in the Rx side). Details of the SCs and ANs that hit this error can be found by reading these registers: MACSEC_<TX/RX>_SC_KEY_INVALID_STATUS0_0, MACSEC_<TX/ RX>_SC_KEY_INVALID_STATUS1_0 To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to the corresponding bit locations of MACSEC_<TX/ RX>_SC_KEY_INVALID_STATUS0_0, MACSEC_<TX/RX>_SC_KEY_INVALID_STATUS1_0. This auto clears MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.< TX/RX>_UNINIT_KEY_SLOT register field. Secure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Secure Register Access Violation This occurs when a non-TZ entity tries to access TZ register space in MACsec. The error is logged in MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0. SECURE_REG_VIOL register field. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 to MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0. SECURE_REG_VIOL register field. Secure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Tx Lookup Miss Interrupt This event occurs when there is no hit in both Tx BYPASS and Tx SC_INDEX LUTs.

MACsec Programming Guidelines This event can assert a secure interrupt if MACSEC_CONTROL0.TX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=0. The error is logged in MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.TX_LKUP_MISS register field. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in the MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.TX_LKUP_MISS register field. Secure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Rx Lookup Miss Interrupt This event occurs when there is no hit in Rx BYPASS LUT. This event can assert a secure interrupt if MACSEC_CONTROL0.RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR=0. The error is logged in MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.RX_LKUP_MISS register field. To clear the status and de-assert the interrupt: Write 1 in the MACSEC_INTERRUPT_STATUS0_0.RX_LKUP_MISS register field. Secure interrupt is de-asserted if there is no other pending event. Handling Safety Interrupts Safety Interrupts are controlled using following registers. MACSEC_INTERRUPT_MASK1_0. SFTY_ERR_UNCORR_INT_EN Status for the Safety Interrupts can be monitored using following registers. MACSEC_INTERRUPT_COMMON_STATUS_0. MSEC_SFTY_ERR_INTR Run Time Reset Assertion Flow There are metastability concerns when reset is applied to MAC or MACsec block during run time. To make sure that there is no metastability concern in these cases, follow the flow defined in the "Reset Special Cases" section.
#### 10.7.3.3 Configuring MACsec LUTs
MACsec contains the list of LUTs in both Tx (Ingress) and Rx (Egress) directions. These LUTs can be programmed using indirect-addressing mode, as explained in the following sections. GCM KEY TABLE LUT SC BYPASS LUT SC INDEX LUT SC STATE LUT SA STATE LUT SC PARAMETER LUT

MACsec Programming Guidelines
##### 10.7.3.3.1 Steps to Configure Tx/Rx KEY TABLE LUT
This is done using GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG, GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0,1,…12] registers. Step1: Configure GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0,1,…12] registers. For write operation, configure the GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0,1,…12] registers with the data that must be written to the LUT at a particular index. For read operation, the GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0,1,…12] registers contains LUT data after the transaction is complete. Ordering requirement: GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0] contains the least significant bits of the LUT data and GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[12] contains most significant bits of the LUT data. (The programming example mentioned in the next section illustrates this requirement.) Step2: Configure the MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0 register: Program MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0.CTLR_SEL=0/1 to select Tx/Rx GCM KEY TABLE LUT. Program MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0.RW=0/1 to read/write from the selected LUT. Program MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0.TABLE_INDEX= index# from/to which data should be written/read from the selected LUT. Program MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0.UPDATE=1 to start the update operation Software should poll for MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0.UPDATE=0 to confirm that the update operation is completed. Example Objective: To load (write) the following content into index 3 of TX_GCM_KEYTABLE_LUT. Table 10.33 TX_GCM_KEYTABLE_LUT ENTRY_VALID[384] HKEY[383:256] SAK[255:0] 0x23457685……64956842 0x14268579….32658925 Steps: Program GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA registers as: GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[12] = 0x1 GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[11] = 0x23457685 …….

MACsec Programming Guidelines GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[8] = 0x64956842 GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[7] = 0x14268579 ……. GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA[0] = 0x32658925 Program GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG fields CTRL_SEL = TX R/W = 1 (WRITE) TABLE_INDEX = 0x3 UPDATE = 1(START) ß--- this bit triggers the hardware to update the LUT Poll for GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG UPDATE field to become 0 (This indicates that LUT is updated successfully).
##### 10.7.3.3.2 Steps to Configure Tx/Rx SA_STATE, SC_PARAM and SC_STATE LUTs
This is done using LUT_CONFIG_0, LUT_DATA [0…6] registers. Step1: Configure the LUT_DATA [0…6] registers: For write operation, configure the LUT_DATA [0…6] registers with the data that must be written into the selected LUT at a particular index. For read operation, the LUT_DATA [0…6] registers contains the LUT data after the transaction is complete. Ordering requirement: LUT_DATA [0] contains the least significant bits and LUT_DATA [6] contains the most significant bits of the LUT data. Step2: Configure the LUT_CONFIG_0 register: Program LUT_CONFIG_0. LUT_SEL= <2=SC_PARAM, 3=SC_STATE> to select the LUT that must be written into/read from. Program LUT_CONFIG_0. CTLR_SEL=0/1 to select Tx/Rx of the preceding LUT type Program LUT_CONFIG_0.RW=0/1 to write/read from the selected LUT Program LUT_CONFIG_0. TABLE_ENTRY_INDEX= index# from/to which data should written/ read from the selected LUT. Program LUT_CONFIG_0. UPDATE=1 to start the update operation Software should poll for LUT_CONFIG_0. UPDATE=0 to confirm that the update operation is completed.

MACsec Programming Guidelines Example Objective: To read data from index 4 of TX_SC_PARAM LUT. Steps: Program the MACSEC_LUT_CONFIG_0 register fields. CONTROL_SEL = 0 (TX) R/W = 0 (READ) LUT_SEL = 2 (SC_PARAM) TABLE_ENTRY_INDEX = 4 UPDATE = 1 (START) Poll until register field MACSEC_LUT_CONFIG_0.UPDATE becomes 0. Read the LUT_DATA[6,…0] registers to see the contents of TX_SC_PARAM LUT at index 2. Various fields in TX_SC_PARAM LUT can be extracted in the following bitmapped way. {key_index_start, PN_max, PN_threshold, TCI, SCI, VLAN_IN_CLR} = {LUT_DATA[0], LUT_DATA[1], LUT_DATA[2], LUT_DATA[3], LUT_DATA[4]};
##### 10.7.3.3.3 Steps to Configure Tx/Rx BYPASS and SC_INDEX LUTs
These LUTs are also configured using indirect addressing mode. The only difference is that VALID bits of each LUT entry are moved from SRAM to Registers. (This change permits software to invalidate quickly all the unused entries during MACsec initial configuration.) Step 1: Write 1 to the corresponding bit locations of the following registers to enable the required Bypass and SC_INDEX LUT entries. MACSEC_TX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID MACSEC_RX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID MACSEC_TX_BYP_LUT_VALID MACSEC_RX_BYP_LUT_VALID Step 2: Configure the MACSEC_LUT_DATA [0…6] registers: For write operation, program the LUT_DATA [0…6] registers with the data that must be written into the selected LUT at a particular index. For read operation, the LUT_DATA [0…6] registers contains LUT data after the transaction is complete. Ordering requirement:

MACsec Programming Guidelines LUT_DATA [0] contains the least significant bits and LUT_DATA [6] contains most significant bits of the LUT data. Step 3: Configure the LUT_CONFIG_0 register: Program LUT_CONFIG_0. LUT_SEL= <0=BYPASS, 1=SC_INDX> to select the LUT that must be written into/read from. Program LUT_CONFIG_0. CTLR_SEL=0/1 to select Tx/Rx of the preceding LUT type Program LUT_CONFIG_0.RW=0/1 to write/read from the selected LUT Program LUT_CONFIG_0. TABLE_ENTRY_INDEX= index# from/to which data should written/ read from the selected LUT. Program LUT_CONFIG_0. UPDATE=1 to start the update operation Software must poll for LUT_CONFIG_0. UPDATE=0 to confirm that the update operation is completed. Example Objective: To write the following data into index 6 of TX_SC_INDX LUT. MAC SA = 112233445566 MAC SA MASK = 88FF00 MAC DA= AABBCCDDEE77 MAC DA MASK = 11AB00 … … Steps: Program MACSEC_TX_SC_INDX_LUT_VALID[6] = 1 Program the MACSEC_LUT_DATA[0…6] register with the preceding write data. For example, program MACSEC_LUT_DATA [0] = 0x33445566 MACSEC_LUT_DATA [1] = 0xFF001122 MACSEC_LUT_DATA [2] = 0xDDEE7788 MACSEC_LUT_DATA [3] = 0x00AABBCC

MACsec Programming Guidelines …. …. Program the MACSEC_LUT_CONFIG_0 register fields. CONTROL_SEL = 0 (TX) R/W = 1 (WRITE) LUT_SEL = 1 (SC_INDX) TABLE_ENTRY_INDEX = 6 UPDATE = 1 (START) Poll until the register field MACSEC_LUT_CONFIG_0.UPDATE becomes 0 to confirm that the data is written successfully into the LUT.
#### 10.7.3.4 Inter-Packet Gap (IPG) Programming in MAC
At the transmit side, packets coming out 1GMAC/XGMAC must have an additional IPG in addition to the minimum IPG (12 bytes) mentioned by the standard. The additional IPG is required to insert MACsec headers in the transmitting packets. It can be either: 24 bytes (8 bytes SECTAG + 16 bytes ICV) 32 bytes (16 bytes SECTAG + 16 bytes ICV)
##### 10.7.3.4.1 1GMAC
MAC_Configuration.IPG[2:0] provides the IPG values defined when EIPGEN=0: Current settings for IPG are: 0x0 (IPG96): 96 bit times IPG 0x1 (IPG88): 88 bit times IPG 0x2 (IPG80): 80 bit times IPG 0x3 (IPG72): 72 bit times IPG 0x4 (IPG64): 64 bit times IPG 0x5 (IPG56): 56 bit times IPG 0x6 (IPG48): 48 bit times IPG 0x7 (IPG40): 40 bit times IPG MAC_Ext_Configuration.EIPGEN: Enables extended IPG When Extended IPG (EIPG) is enabled, then {MAC_Ext_Configuration.EIPG[4:0], MAC_Configuration.IPG[2:0]} à NewIPG[7:0] provides Extended IPG values (in steps of 8 bits): Extended IPG = 96 + NewIPG[7:0]*8 Example: If EIPGEN=1, NewIPG=12, then Extended IPG=96+96=192 or 24B

MACsec Programming Guidelines
##### 10.7.3.4.2 XGMAC
MAC_Tx_configuration.IFP: Enables extended IPG Current settings for IPG[2:0] are: 3'b000: 96 bit times 3'b001: 88 bit times 3'b010: 80 bit times 3'b011: 72 bit times 3'b100: 64 bit times 3'b101: 3'b111: Reserved MAC_Extended_Configuration.EIPG: Provides Extended IPG as defined. When the MAC_Tx_configuration.IFP bit is set, the minimum IPG is increased in steps of 32 bits depending on the programming of the MAC_Extended_Configuration.EIPG field and IPG field in the MAC_Tx_Configuration register. {EIPG,IPG}: Minimum Inter-Packet Gap-->96 + {EIPG,IPG}*32 - - - - - - - 10'h000: 96 bit times 10'h001: 128 bit times 10'h010: 160 bit times 10'h011: 192 bit times 10'h100: 224 bit times ... 10'h3FF: 32832 bit times Example: If {EIPG, IPG}=3, then Extended IPG = 96+3*32=192 bits or 24 B
#### 10.7.3.5 Programming Block Level Firewalls
The MACsec AMAP space is protected using BLFs (Block Level Firewalls). The list of BLFs and the region, which each BLF is protecting is shown in the following diagram. MACsec Tx/Rx KEY TABLE LUTs are protected by MACSEC_TZ BLF. Hence, software should program MACSEC_TZ BLF to permit access only from TZ entity. As a second-level protection, MACsec IP also does the TZ check, (for example, check if the master that is accessing TZ space, has PPROT[1]=0). This second level protection is guarded by the fuse input to MACsec inside the IP. All other MACsec LUTs are protected by MACSEC_RM_TX_BYP BLF. Hence software should program MACSEC_RM_TX_BYP BLF to permit access either from TZ entity or from an RM entity based on the platform. Software should program MACSEC_RM_RX_BYP BLF, MACSEC_RM_CFG BLF, MACSEC_RM_ERR_BLF to permit access only from RM entity.

MACsec Programming Guidelines
**Figure 10.66 Block Level Firewalls**
#### 10.7.3.6 Global Configuration Register Fields Description
Configuration bit Reset value Comments MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.TX_ENB By default, MACsec Tx controller will be disabled. (Packets coming to MACsec Tx get bypassed) This bit should be programmed to 1 to enable MACsec in transmit direction. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_ENB By default, MACsec Rx controller will be disabled. (Packets coming to MACsec Rx get bypassed) This bit should be programmed to 1 to enable MACsec in receive direction.

MACsec Programming Guidelines Configuration bit Reset value Comments MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.VALIDATE_FR AMES[22:21] STRICT Used in receive direction during SC lookup stage. Based on this setting and various error scenarios, respective counters are incremented and also packet is sent to MAC with corrupted CRC or good CRC. 0 = DISABLED: ICV check is disabled. SecTag and ICV fields are removed from the frame before forwarding it to the next module. 1 = CHECK: ICV check is done. And the InPktsInValid counter is updated based on ICV check result. Packet is sent without corrupting CRC to MAC. (after removing SecTag and ICV) 2 = STRICT: ICV check is done. If ICV check fails, the frame is dropped (CRC of the frame is corrupted) and InPktsNotValid counter is updated. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.TX_LOOKUP_ MISS DROP When the packet does not hit any of the Bypass or SC-Index LUT, packet will be dropped or bypassed based on this bit. 0 = DROP: Corrupt the packet on tables lookup miss. 1 = BYPASS: Bypass the packet on tables lookup miss. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_LOOKUP_ MISS DROP When there is a Bypass LUT miss, packet is corrupted or bypassed based on this bit. Note: This bit is applicable only for Bypass LUT and not SC index LuT. 0 = DROP: Corrupt the packet on bypass tables lookup miss. 1 = BYPASS: Bypass the packet on bypass tables lookup miss. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_REPLAY_ PROT_EN ENABLE Replay Protection can be enabled or disabled using this bit. 0 = DISABLE: Disable replay protection. 1 = ENABLE: Enable replay protection. MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.TX_LKP_MIS S_NON_SECURE_INTR SECURE_INTR When Tx lookup miss event occurs, hardware will assert secure/non-secure intr based on this bit. 0 = SECURE_INTR 1 = NON_SECURE_INTR MACSEC_CONTROL0_0.RX_LKP_MIS S_NON_SECURE_INTR SECURE_INTR When Rx lookup miss event occurs, hardware will assert secure/non-secure intr based on this bit. 0 = SECURE_INTR 1 = NON_SECURE_INTR

MACsec Programming Guidelines Configuration bit Reset value Comments MACSEC_CONTROL1_0. INT_LPBK_MODE Loopback disabled. Internal Loopback mode. When this bit is set, MACsec Tx output lines will be connected to MACsec Rx input lines internally as shown in Block Diagram. The loopback is implemented in the MACsec Wrapper at: RGMII interface for ETHER_QOS MACsec instance. XGMII interface for MGBE MACsec instances. 0 = DISABLE: Disable Loopback. 1 = ENABLE: Enable Loopback. MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.TX_MTU_CH ECK_ENB MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.RX_MTU_CH ECK_ENB MACsec Transmit and Receive Maximum Transmission Unit Check control bits (Controlled separately) Note: When 1GMAC and XGMAC do not perform an MTU Check, this functionality is added in MACSEC. 0 = DISABLE: Disable MTU check. 1 = ENABLE: Enable MTU check. MACSEC_CONTROL1_0.TX_LUT_PRIO RITY MACsec Transmit SC and Bypass LUTs' priority control 0 = SC: SC Index LUT has the priority over Bypass LUT. 1 = BYPASS: Bypass LUT has the priority over SC-Index LUT. MACSEC_GCM_AES_CONTROL_0. RX_AES_MODE[1:0] AES-128 bit MACsec Receive AES Mode of operation 0 = AES128: AES-128bit Key 1 = Reserved 2 = AES256: AES-256bit Key 3 = Reserved MACSEC_GCM_AES_CONTROL_0. TX_AES_MODE[1:0] AES-128 bit MACsec Transmit AES Mode of operation 0 = AES128: AES-128bit Key 1 = AES192: AES-192bit Key, Not supported 2 = AES256: AES-256bit Key 3 = UNDEFINED: This setting is reserved. MACSEC_TX_MTU_LEN_0[15:0] MACSEC_RX_MTU_LEN_0[15:0] 0x3fff MTU_LENGTH_THRESHOLD: 0 is illegal. Non-Zero value of X indicates packet length. Greater than X will be treated as violating MTU check.

MACsec Registers
### 10.7.4 MACsec Registers
MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_CONFIG_0 GCM KeyTable Registers Indirect Addressing Access: Register controls for programming the Key tables GCM KeyTable Config Register Offset: 0x0 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: YT194 Shadow: N Secure: Trust Zone Protected SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0xxx,xx00,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0,0000) Bit Reset Description 0x0 UPDATE: Key Table Configuration Update control SW has to trigger by writing Logic 1 to the UPDATE field after programming DATA and other config fields. Poll for the value to become Logic0 to ensure the operation is complete. 0 = DONE :Update operation is done or No update operation is initiated 1 = START :Start the Update operation 0x0 CTLR_SEL: MACSEC Controller selection (Transmit or Receive) 0 = TX :MACSEC Transmitter 1 = RX :MACSEC Receiver 0x0 RW: Key Table access direction 0 = READ :Read entries from GCM KeyTable 1 = WRITE :Write to GCM KeyTable 4:0 0x0 TABLE_INDEX: Key Table slot Address or Index where the Key would be written MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA_0 The following register set holds the data value for KeyTable.Format of the data resembles exactly the KeyTable format. This is an array of 13 identical register entries; the register fields below apply to each entry. Full register list is: MACSEC_GCM_KEYTABLE_DATA_<i>, among which <i> belongs to <0..12>. Offset: 0x4,..,0x34

MACsec Registers Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N Secure: Trust Zone Protected SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 31:0 0x0 DATA MACSEC_MAC_CONTROL_0 Adding register bits to control CRC mask bits for MAC The lock bit is used as a mask for the register field which is being protected. In order to change the configuration of the register bit, the lock bit should be disabled until the required functionality is complete. Programming the lock bit to 1 will override the register fields with the secure value (i.e., in case of DCRCC, CRC will be checked for all packets) Offset: 0x4c Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N Secure: Trust Zone Protected SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000007 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,x111) Bit Reset Description 0x1 RXQ_RSF_LOCK: Set to 0 to configure EQOS_MTL_Q[n]_MTL_RXQ[n]_OPERATION_MODE_0.RSF n={0..7} for EQOS Set to 0 to configure MGBE_DWCXG_MTL_TCQ[n]_MTL_RXQ[n]_OPERATION_MODE_0.RSF n={0..9} for MGBE 0x1 RXQ_FEP_LOCK: Set to 0 to configure EQOS_MTL_Q[n]_MTL_RXQ[n]_OPERATION_MODE_0.FEP n={0..7} for EQOS Set to 0 to configure MGBE_DWCXG_MTL_TCQ[n]_MTL_RXQ[n]_OPERATION_MODE_0.FEF n={0..9} for MGBE 0x1 DCRCC_LOCK: Set to 0 to configure EQOS_MAC_MAC_EXT_CONFIGURATION_0.DCRCC for EQOS Set to 0 to configure MGBE_DWCXG_CORE_MAC_RX_CONFIGURATION_0.DCRCC for MGBE

MACsec Registers MACSEC_RX_ICV_ERROR_CONTROL_0 MACSEC Ingress ICV failures Threshold register Offset: 0x4000 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00003fff (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0011,1111,1111,1111) Bit Reset Description 15:0 0x3fff ICV_ERROR_THRESHOLD: When Threshold count is reached, MACSEC sets ICV Error event and generates an interrupt if interrupt is enabled. Setting "0" means no reporting of ICV Errors. Should program with Non zero value to get the ICV Error interrupt. MACSEC_INTERRUPT_COMMON_STATUS_0 MACSEC Common (TX and RX controller) Interrupt Status Register This status register will have a status bit that is OR(All MACSEC TX interrupts). Similarly a status bit for OR(All MACSEC RX Interrupts). This will help to quickly identify the source of interrupt whether it is MACSEC TX or MACSEC RX controller. Offset: 0x4004 Read/Write: RO Parity Protection: N Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,x000) Bit Reset Description 0x0 MSEC_SFTY_ERR_INTR: MACSEC Safety Interrupt status 0 = UNSET 1 = SET 0x0 MSEC_RX_INTR: MACSEC RX controller Interrupt status 0 = UNSET 1 = SET

MACsec Registers Following register indicates the SCs that got into Error state due to various events like Invalid AN (means SC has reached a state where the new AN is not available). Invalid AN state is reached typically becuse SW has not enabled the new AN in advance and previous AN is exhuasted (i.e. PN Max has reached and new packet has come). MACsec Registers Bit Reset Description 0x0 REPLAY_ERROR: Replay Protection Check failed. The PN of just received frame is smaller than PN of last received frame or outside allowed window. 0 = UNSET 1 = SET 0x0 MTU_CHECK_FAIL: MTU Check failed. The Incoming packet (from LINE side module to MACSEC) length is greater than programmed MTU Length 0 = UNSET 1 = SET 0x0 AES_GCM_BUF_OVF: AES_GCM_BUF overflow occurred. Buffer overflow event should not get triggered during normal course of operation. 0 = UNSET 1 = SET 0x0 MAC_CRC_ERROR: CRC error is detected in the incoming frame (from LINE side module to MACSEC) 0 = UNSET 1 = SET 0x0 PN_EXHAUSTED: Packet Number of SA/AN is exhausted 0 = UNSET 1 = SET MACSEC_RX_INTERRUPT_SET_0 MACSEC Ingress Interrupt Set Register This is a write-only register which can be used to set the interrupt status bit. A write to this register causes the bits in RX_INTERRUPT_STATUS register to be set if the corresponding bit in write data is 1'b1. Read always returns 'h0. MACsec Registers Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00500000 (0bxxxx,xxx0,0101,0xx0,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0xx0) Bit Reset Description 0x0 TX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR: When TX look up miss event occurs, hw will assert secure/non-secure intr based on this bit. Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = SECURE_INTR 1 = NON_SECURE_INTR 0x0 RX_LKP_MISS_NON_SECURE_INTR: When RX look up miss event occurs, hw will assert secure/non-secure intr based on this bit. Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = SECURE_INTR 1 = NON_SECURE_INTR 22:21 0x2 VALIDATE_FRAMES: MACSEC Receive Frame Validate control Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DISABLED :ICV check is disabled. SecTag and ICV fields are removed from the frame before forwarding it to the next module 1 = CHECK :ICV check is done. And the InPktsInValid counter is updated based on ICV check result. 2 = STRICT :ICV check is done. If ICV check fails, the frame is dropped (CRC of the frame is corrupted) and InPktsNotValid counter is updated. 0x1 RX_REPLAY_PROT_EN: MACSEC Receive Frame Replay Protection enable control Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DISABLE :Disable Replay Protection 1 = ENABLE :Enable Replay Protection 0x0 RX_LOOKUP_MISS: MACSEC Receive: Select an action for Bypass LookUP tables miss (No matching entry found in the Bypass LUT). This bit is applicable only for Bypass LuT and not SC index LuT Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DROP :Corrupt the packet on bypass tables lookup miss 1 = BYPASS :Bypass the packet on bypass tables lookup miss 0x0 RX_ENB: MACSEC Receive Controller enable bit. Bypasses the MACSEC RX controller Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DISABLE :Bypasses MACSEC Receive Controller 1 = ENABLE :Enables MACSEC Receive Controller 0x0 TX_LOOKUP_MISS: MACSEC Transmit: Select an action for LookUP tables miss (No matching entry found in both Bypass and SC-Index LUTs). Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DROP :Corrupt the packet on tables lookup miss 1 = BYPASS :Bypass the packet on tables lookup miss

MACsec Registers Bit Reset Description 0x0 TX_ENB: MACSEC Transmit Controller enable bit. Bypasses the MACSEC TX controller Reset_Domain: Secure_Reset. 0 = DISABLE :Disables MACSEC Transmit Controller 1 = ENABLE :Enables MACSEC Transmit Controller MACSEC_LUT_CONFIG_0 Indirect Addressing access: Register controls for programming the LookUP tables Offset: 0xd004 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0b0xxx,xx00,xxxx,x000,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0,0000) Bit Reset Description 0x0 UPDATE: LookUP Table Configuration Update control SW has to trigger by writing Logic 1 to the UPDATE field after programming DATA and other config fields. Poll for the value to become Logic0 to ensure the operation is complete. 0 = DONE :Update operation is done or No update operation is initiated 1 = START :Start the Update operation 0x0 CTLR_SEL: MACSEC Controller selection (Transmit or Receiver) 0 = TX :MACSEC Transmitter 1 = RX :MACSEC Receiver 0x0 RW: Table access direction 0 = READ :Read entries from LookUP Table 1 = WRITE :Write to LookUP Table 18:16 0x0 LUT_SEL: LookUP table Selection control 0 = BYPASS 1 = SC_INDX 2 = SC_PARAM 3 = SC_STATE 4 = SA_STATE 4:0 0x0 TABLE_ENTRY_INDEX: Table slot Address or Index where an entry would be written

MACsec Registers MACSEC_LUT_DATA_0 MACSEC LUT Data register Following register-set holds the data value for a LookUP table. Format of the data resembles the exact table that is to be programmed. This is an array of 7 identical register entries; the register fields below apply to each entry. Full register list is: MACSEC_LUT_DATA_<i>, among which <i> belongs to <0..6>. When this bit is set to ENABLE, MACSEC TX output lines will be connectd to MACSEC RX input lines internally. It takes 1us for this bit to take effect inside the MACSEC logic. This bit is also used as the loopback FIFO flush bit and needs to be deasserted for 2us for the flush operation to complete. 0 = DISABLE :Disable Loopback 1 = ENABLE :Enable Loopback 0x0 RX_MTU_CHECK_ENB: MACSEC Receive Maximum Transmission Unit Check Control bit 0 = DISABLE :Disable MTU check 1 = ENABLE :Enable MTU check 0x0 TX_LUT_PRIORITY: MACSEC Transmit SC and Bypass LUTs priority Control 0 = SC :SC Index LUT has the priority over Bypass LUT 1 = BYPASS :Bypass LUT has the priority over SC-Index LUT 0x0 TX_MTU_CHECK_ENB: MACSEC Transmit Maximum Transmission Unit Check Control bit 0 = DISABLE :Disable MTU check 1 = ENABLE :Enable MTU check MACSEC_GCM_AES_CONTROL_0

MACsec Registers Bit Reset Description 31:16 0x8e NUM_ERR: Number of errors connected to this collator. This is passed as a build time option to the plugin 5:0 0x5 NUM_ERR_SLICES: Number of error slices supported by this error collator, does not include the GlobalSpace and is derived by ceil (NUM_ERR/32). SW shall first read this register to determine the number of slices and read the required number of Error_Status registers . MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_SWRESET_0 Offset: 0xf004 Read/Write: WO Parity Protection: N Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0) Bit Reset Description 0x0 SWRST: 1'b1 : Issue a SW reset to the Error Collator. This will reset all the registers(Except SCR), counters and logic of the Error Collator. SW can use this bit to flush errors logged into the error collator for ex, after Boot, SC7/8 exit. 1'b0 : Do nothing, reset value. This bit is auto-cleared. MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_MISSIONERR_TYPE_0 Offset: 0xf008 Read/Write: RO Parity Protection: N Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000005 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xx00,0101)

MACsec Registers Bit Reset Description 5:0 0x5 CODE: This register indicates the fault code of the error line based on the value of MISSIONERR_INDEX Register. This can be used by a fault handling agent to triage an error without requiring device-specific code.The possible values of this field are: 6'd0 : None 6'd1 : Parity Error on internal data path 6'd2 : ECC SEC Error on internal data path 6'd3 : ECC DED Error on internal data path 6'd4 : Comparator Error 6'd5 : Register Parity Error 6'd6 : Parity Error from on-chip SRAM/Fifo 6'd7 : ECC SEC Error from on-chip SRAM/Fifo 6'd8 : ECC DED Error from on-chip SRAM/Fifo 6'd9 : Clock Monitor Error 6'd10 : Voltage Error 6'd11 : Temperature Error 6'd12 : CRC Error on internal data path 6'd16 : SW Corrected Error 6'd17 : SW Uncorrected Error 6'd18 : SW Generic Error 6'd20 : ECC SED Error on internal data path 6'd21 : ECC SED Error from on-chip SRAM/Fifo 6'd32 : Other HW Corrected Error 6'd33 : Other HW Uncorrected Error All other values : Reserved MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_CURRENT_COUNTER_VALUE_0 Offset: 0xf00c Read/Write: RO Parity Protection: N Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxx0,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 8:0 0x0 VALUE: Provides the current value of the counter corresponding to the error in MissionErr_Index Register. Default provides the value of error 0 counter. Bit[8] is the ovrerflow bit post which the counter saturates and does not counter further. MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_MISSIONERR_USERVALUE_0 Offset: 0xf010 Read/Write: RO Parity Protection: N Shadow: N

MACsec Registers SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0xdead0000 (0b1101,1110,1010,1101,0000,0000,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 31:0 0xdead0000 VALUE: Reflects the value on the error_<i>_user when error_<i>_pulse = MissionError. Only the user signals corresponding to the first error_<i>_pulse only will b elatched.Subsequent values will be dropped. The signals will get latched only when ERRSLICE<n>_MISSIONERR_STATUS is CLEAR. IPs must tie off the unused bits of this signals to 0, if unused. MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_MISSIONERR_INDEX_0 Offset: 0xf014 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 7:0 0x0 IDX: BINARY Encoded. For error number 32, register should be programmed with value 0x20. Write to this register with Error number will update:
- MISSIONERR_TYPE Register with the Error-Code for the Error.
- CURRENT_COUNTER_VALUE Register with the error's SEC/DED Counter.
- MISSIONERR_USERVALUE with value of the first error_<i>_user signal.
SW can use this to trage the error. number shall update the MISSIONERR_TYPE register with the error code and the Current_Counter_Value register with the value of the errors SEC/DED counter. SW can use this register to triage the error. MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_CORRECTABLE_THRESHOLD_0 Offset: 0xf018 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0000,0000)

MACsec Registers Bit Reset Description 7:0 0x0 COUNT: Threshold value for all SEC Fault Reporting Units connected to this error collator. SEC Errors are logged once the threshold is reached and the overflow bit is set. 7'b0 : Log SEC error after receiving 1 Error. 7'b1 : Log SEC error after receiving 2 Errors. ... 7'bFF : Log SEC error after receiving 256 Errors. MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_MISSIONERR_INJECT_UNLOCK_0 Offset: 0xf01c Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: N Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,xxxx,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 7:0 0x0 VALUE: Writes to ERRSLICE_XXX_MISSIONERR_INJECT registers are disabled until this register is written with a value of 0xE1. This is to prevent an inadvertent safety error injection in the safety plugin due to: 1. A fault on ERRSLICE_XXX_MISSIONERR_INJECT register itself. 2. Erroneous SW. The register shall be written with a value of 0x0 to reestablish the lock after user has completed the error injection testing. 0xE1 : Unlock the MISSIONERR_INJECT Register 0x0 : Lock the MISSIONERR_INJECT Register 0 = LOCK 225 = UNLOCK MACSEC_ERRCOLLATOR_ERRSLICE0_MISSIONERR_ENABLE_0 Offset: 0xf030 Read/Write: R/W Parity Protection: Y Shadow: N SCR Protection: 0 Reset: 0xffffffeb (0b1111,1111,1111,1111,1111,1111,111x,1x11)
